< text>
My fiance and I have been staying here for almost a month as we are waiting for our apartment to be ready. We have 2 well-trained, well-behaved, friendly service animals. They are a Husky mix and under 2 years old. Some time after I paid this morning, I received a call in my room from the manager, Sal, saying that we would have to check out  in the morning that they were not going to extend our stay anymore because it was brought to his attention that we had dogs in our room. I said "yes, they are service animals". He said , "well unfortunately we are not going to be able to extend your stay. You should have told us in the beginning."

Well, Sal, per the law I do NOT have to tell you ahead of time that I have service animals. Kicking us out because we have service animals is discrimination. What you are saying is that I have to tell you about my disability ahead of time in order to stay in  your establishment. If my dogs were a wheelchair, would the same apply? If my dogs were a home health aide, would I have to tell you about him/her ahead of time? So why do I have to tell  you that I have service animals ahead of time? According to the American Disabilities Act, no such notice is required and it is unlawful for you to kick me out because of my service animals and because I didn't give you advance notice I was checking in with them.

We are also Platinum Wyndham Rewards Members. You would think that being Platinum members (when Diamond is the only level left) of your loyalty program, your company would show a little more loyalty and not just discard us like yesterday's news. Obviously we have been spending money here to get to that level. I am extremely dismayed at being treated in such a manner. I expect such treatment from the dirt-bag motel down the street but I did not expect it from an establishment with the Wyndham name, especially since you boast "SERVICE ANIMALS ARE WELCOME" for all your hotels! That really should read "SERVICE ANIMALS ARE WELCOME ONLY IF YOU GET OUR PERMISSION IN ADVANCE TO HAVE ONE". Your company is too big, too well-known for you to be this ignorant of the laws and to actively participate in discrimination against anyone particularly of the disabled. I'm ashamed of you and will pursue this issue as far as I need to .

In addition, the front desk prior to this had informed us that it was coming up on 28 days that we had been staying here. Hotels try to do this to circumvent the law that would give one tenancy if staying in the hotel for 30 consecutive days because if you check out and then check back in the next day, you have to wait another 30 days to get tenant rights. If you move out every 28 days, you never achieve tenancy. This game that your hotel, along with several other hotels, is playing  is illegal and could result in your hotel being fined $500 each time it does this. $500 does not sound like a lot once but if everyone who you did it to came forward, I imagine it would add up to some hefty fines.

So I will not remain silent. I will tell whoever will listen that Days Inn in Carlsbad on 3700 Pio Pico Dr. participates in the "musical rooms" game to try to circumvent the tenancy law, WHICH IS ILLEGAL and they are also discriminatory, kicking people out because of known service animals brought into their establishment WHICH IS ALSO ILLEGAL.

You guys have some explaining to do!</text>

< review>
I sincerely wish I could give zero stars for their Glendale, CA location. Avoid Zeus at all costs.

*CLEANLINESS*
Upon checking into our unit we found it had not been cleaned. The surfaces had not been wiped down, on the carpeting we found a used band-aid and dried vomit as well as black market HGH (Trenbolone Acetate) hidden in our electric box and what we later figured out was the tip of a needle. The filth would be upsetting under normal circumstances but during Covid they're frankly inexcusable. My wife is immunocompromised so these all pose a very real danger to her health. This company does not take Covid seriously.

*FALSE CHARGES*
We had to extend our stay (we're waiting on construction at our home) and Zeus entered our updated checkout date incorrectly. We already paid a service fee when we updated our booking, however we were pressured to pay an additional service fee, despite the error being on their part. As of today they still refuse to refund us for their mistake.

*FALSE ADVERTISING*
Our unit was not as advertised. We brought this up to Airbnb and were told they would not help us. There was massive construction done outside our unit nearly every workday of our stay. I have numerous photos and videos as evidence. When we reached we were told that the work was "minimal", however there was scaffolding outside our unit (blocking our view) and the work was constant with the exception of the holidays. We've been out of the unit for several weeks and can see the construction is still ongoing when we drive by. Do not believe the pictures of your room when you book.

*PARKING*
In addition, they've nearly had our car towed on multiple occasions because they did not include a parking pass when we checked in and told us the wrong place to park when we asked for clarification. When we complained about nearly being towed, they forced us to park on the roof out of spite--past 70-100 empty covered spots. This company is petty.</review>

<Text>One of the most baffling and frustrating customer experiences I can remember. The pricing model is stunningly opaque. This is compounded by website errors that create a mismatch between quoted prices on the same unit for the same dates on the same page.

Pricing is algorithmically driven, and appears to have features of a Dutch price auction (the kind they use to sell tulips), where prices start high and decrease over time until someone purchases. This type of dynamic pricing for consumers works in low-stakes settings, like an Uber ride or weekend rental. It's exceptionally frustrating with longer term rentals, where visibility into rent 2+ months out is non-existant, and where the stakes for waiting vs. renting immediately can be $1-3K/month.

I'm sure the units are lovely (a leap of faith, as no viewings allowed before move-in), but buying something should be easy as pie. The fact that it's this difficult to get a hold on the "true" price gives me significant doubts about what it will be like to deal with this company as a tennant. If this is what "living-as-a-service" means, I'm not sure that it's a service I want.<//Text>< Pictures>

<text>Ah, Zeus Living.  Hardly.

Precisely the opposite.  These guys are very, very incompetent.  They have severe issues with internal communication, and they are constantly, repeatedly, repetitively screwing up as a result of it.

And guess who gets to enjoy the brunt of it?  Why you, the client!

When I showed up to get into my unit:

1) The "welcome doc" provided had no links to important videos, such as "how to find the keybox".

No worries, I thought.  There are text instructions too!  Yet I looked, and looked, and looked -- and no boxes were to be found.

2) After calling Zeus, and finally getting someone on the line, videos were provided to me.  Those same videos?  Showed keyboxes where I had looked -- but no, they were not there.

3) I was told a technician would be coming out to help.  I explained that I was in a convertible, and gave the make and model.  There was no other such car anywhere... yet when the technician showed up?

He walked past my car several times.  Why  did I not approach him? Well, lots of people were walking by.  That's why he knew how to find me, by.. you know, looking for my car.

He then was incapable of calling me.  Why?  Because there was a "strange message" on the phone.  Said strange message was "press 5 to continue", it's there to prevent telemarketers.  Had he pressed 5?  Why, I'd have answered!

4) After moving into the apartment, within minutes I noticed that 1/2 the place had no power.

When checking, it became clear that a breaker was damaged... and more so?  That someone at Zeus had been investigating it.. yet there I was, living in a unit with 1/2 the outlets, lights, the TV, and the heat non-functional.

5) Zeus.. eventually moved me to another unit.  Of course, I was then repeatedly spammed with "You haven't paid!" for the new unit, and the OLD unit still showed as rented on their website.  For days.

I finally contacted them, saving them potentially loads of cash -- after all, you can't rent a unit that isn't showing as available.. and they fixed this simple issue.

--

There are loads, and loads, and loads of other issues just like this.  They all boil own to Zeus Living have severe, extreme, MASSIVE issues with internal communication.

If you look at the list above, it's all about information going missing.

Meanwhile, this is supposedly Zeus's strength, to leverage how data is stored, and how units are rented, to enhance the experience a customer receives.  Instead, they seem to have no viable way to store information, no way to communicate between departments...

And even when they DO communicate, information is lost.

I'm sure someone at Zeus will reply to this, with an inane "Please contact us so we can help!", which is a falsehood.  They won't help, they can't.  They're inept.

They may also provide explanations for all of the above.  One favourite of theirs, is that they "haven't been" to most of their units, because they have "over 600" of them.

Uh, so?  The whole point is to develop, and employ a streamlined process that enables them to manage that "large number" of units... which clearly they aren't.

Stay clear of them, they're a disaster.

Oh right!  To follow up!

Zeus's model seems to be to rent units where landlords "want in".  Yet how does this work?

Why, it's simple:

- landlord has problems renting unit
- a deal is reached -- and one that gives Zeus Living a discount on rental pricing
- Zeus then furnishes, and rents it out

You see, these apartments/houses are ones that won't command top dollar, that are hard to rent for the landlord... because they have PROBLEMS.

Take my unit.  It's right beside a freeway, next to a municipal workyard, beside a construction site.

<review>I don't give out 5 star ratings very often, but Brad Stoner Painting earned one when they painted our house.  I had no idea who to get to paint our house, so I did a search on Yelp. Brad's reviews were all very good, so I decided to go with him. Brad operated his business in a very professional manner from the beginning bid process all the way through to the end. Brad and his painters were punctual every day, and they were finished on time. Brad's price was good; not the lowest, certainly not the most expensive, and very reasonable.

Our house is an 85 year-old craftsman house requiring lots of attention to detail, and the painters (in particular Freddy) did just that. An amazing job! < text>
I see Brad Stoner Painting has a five star rating. In order for me to believe those are all true reviews, I would have to believe I'm the only one in the universe unhappy with them. And that's hard to buy considering how unprofessional they were.
Brad contracted to paint my house July 5th-8th. But it wasn't done on the 8th or the 9th or the 10th or the 11th. Not really surprising since he had one person working on it the majority if the time. And one guy had to borrow tools from me and I had to get my ladder to help him lift my patio cover back up.
Contract said they would sand, prime and paint the metalwork on my closed in front porch. But they skipped the sanding and priming steps. Instead they just globed on paint. It looked horrible and was peeling before they walked off the job. I pointed it out, but the guy left anyway. I pointed problems out on a daily basis, but they ignored them.
Brad knew before I signed the contract that I was leaving the country for three weeks starting July 13th. When his guy walked iff the job, without telling me he was leaving, leaving my front gate lock unworkable and all the poor workmanship, I emailed Brad with a long itemized list of what still had to be done. He said to pay him 1/2 and let him know when I returned so they could finish. I told him he could work while I was gone, but he said no. That seemed odd to me that he wouldn't want to get it done, off his books and paid. Red flags started going up for me.
When I retuned I made contact. Brad, a supervisor and two workman came. I had put tape in a lot of places where work needed to be done, (poorly cut lines, the horrible mess they made of my metalwork, old paint showing through, messy paint smeared, smudged, dripped on the aluminum window casings, etc) Both Brad and the supervisor agreed that all the things needed ti be fixed and that they could do it that day.
But at the end if that day, it wasn't done. The next day 3 guys showed up and I was sure they would knick it out. After all, it was the first time 3 workers came.  Shortly after arriving though, two disappeared, leaving one person. 4 hours later one of the missing workers showed up, but then both guys left for the day about           1 P. M.
I sent Brad an email, voicing my dissatisfaction and asking him to please send enough people to finish the job the next day. I also told him, if it wasn't done by 4 P.M. the next day (3rd day of finish work, 10th day of the 4 day paint job) I would not pay him. He responded "Ok"
That didn't get the job done. 2 guys showed up and...Whatever they did, it wasn't painting my house, because AGAIN, they left early without finishing.
Poor management, amateur painters, no pride in workmanship, lying, part time work to do a full time job and just plain not caring add up to an unhappy experience.
Twice I was offered money to "forget it". He offered me money in exchange for a signed document waiving my right to free speech. Maybe that's why all his reviews are good; he pays people to keep quiet.
But I have integrity and could not live with myself if I did not warn people about what might happen if they hire Brad Stoner Painting.
My theory is that they figured a 65 year old woman, with no husband, wouldn't notice their poor workmanship and that they could walk off with their $3800 without putting in the time and effort to do a $3800 job.
These are the facts, but not the whole story. I have left out how much of my time was wasted, how much work I lost because I had to babysit these guys. How much anguish I went through having to get up at midnight to let my roommate in after the guy screwed up my lock. I had to find a locksmith and watch him while he put my lock back together properly.
And all the days they were "working" , I couldn't open my front door to get air because they took the screens and lock off my front porch and left it like that. So 11 days and nights of running the AC.
These are the facts, without exaggeration. BEWARE IF BRAD STONER PAINTING!<//text>

< Text>
Good, affordable food, right on the beach. Very cozy vibe. I like the booths. If you‚Äôre looking for an affordable family friendly option with good servers this is an excellent choice. The only reason for 4 stars, rather than 5 is the decor (inside and outside) seems to be from 1982. Throw a fresh coat of paint on this place and it would be awesome. That being said, I love the Blackened Chicken Sandwich (or the Surfin Bird sandwich), it is delicious. They also serve breakfast all day and have daily specials, including an all you can eat spaghetti day. Definitely a worthwhile restaurant choice, not fancy, but friendly, affordable, and tasty.</Text>

Scotty‚Äôs is a classic, and a landmark of the Hermosa Beach strand.

My family stays at the Sea Sprite Motel right next-door, and this place has been a favorite of ours for years.   The staff is always friendly, the food is pretty basic - but good. They are slammed during summer months, but my favorite time to come is in the wee hours of the morning for endless hot coffee, good hot breakfast, and just staring out at the beach.

Today I‚Äôm here on a business trip and I brought my computer with me.  It‚Äôs the beginning of December so the beach goers today are presumably all locals - and the people watching is pretty amazing.

I highly recommend for a cozy and consistently good, diner-on-the-strand experience!</text>

< review>
This place is actually one of my new favorite places for a brunch. Nice location by the beach and those tables by the window facing the beach are heaven. I've been to this place twice since i found it through Yelp.
First experience (May 6) was amazing, my partner and i had marinated tri-tip with 2 eggs, potatoes and bread plus coffee and OJ. Our server was Candis and she was pretty nice and attentive
Second experience (May 21), we ordered exactly the same and it was great as usual but we were really disappointed with the service. Our server was Rachel, she didn't even say hi...grumpy when she took the order, MIA & the worst part was she dropped the check while my partner was still eating without even asking us first if we wanted anything else. We were thinking to order a bottle sparkling wine. My partner was mad because of this so we just paid the bill and moved to Hennessey's Tavern to have some drink.

Updated September 17, 2017:
Today I had brunch here with my partner, we both ordered the same food again and again everytime we eat here. It was 2 over medium eggs with medium rare tri tip, home fries, sourdough toast, coffee and OJ. Our server was Jessy and she was so attentive and friendly. We really had a good time enjoying our brunch facing the beach plus good service from Jessy. Well for that reason Scotty's deserves to get more stars :)

PS: This place provides private parking space for customers.</review>

<Rating>4< /Rating><text>A local's favorite diner type restaurant virtually on the sand. I've patronized this local gem for breakfast/ lunch for years. Nothing fancy. Food is freshly prepared, made to order and the servers are friendly.  A favorite is the breakfast quesadilla... ask for extra Spanish sauce.

<user>110353391094333959585</user><name>D. Moe</name>< time>
1517763103291</time>
<rating>4</rating>< Text>
A local's favorite diner type restaurant virtually on the sand. I've patronized this local gem for breakfast/ lunch for years. Nothing fancy. Food is freshly prepared, made to order and the servers are friendly.  A favorite is the breakfast quesadilla... ask for extra Spanish sauce.

The patio portion has skylights and virtually floor to ceiling windows that slide open allowing in the ocean breeze & sounds of the beach & strand. The view is directly, eye-level with the strand & sand allowing diners to watch the passers go by and volleyball players practice on the courts toward the south of the restaurant. (The view is better when the County doesn't have a giant storm-protective sand berm sitting between the restaurant & the ocean. Also, I recall when the section of beach directly out the windows & immediately south of the pier didn't contain the public restrooms & showers and wasn't utilized as an equipment & service vehicle parking area.) The view was nicer when it used to be just sand, volleyball courts, beach goers & the Pacific.< /Text>
